href="/wiki/2RN_(RT%C3%89_Networks)" title="2RN (RT\xc3\x89 Networks)">2RN</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label" style="padding-right: 0.5em;">Website</th><td class="infobox-data" style="line-height: 1.35em;"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.rte.ie">www.rte.ie</a></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Raidi\xc3\xb3 Teilif\xc3\xads \xc3\x89ireann</b> (<b>RT\xc3\x89</b>)<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> (<small>Irish pronunciation:&#160;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Irish" title="Help:IPA/Irish">[\xcb\x88\xc9\xbe\xcb\xa0ad\xca\xb2o\xcb\x90 \xcb\x88t\xca\xb2\xc9\x9bl\xca\xb2\xc9\x99f\xca\xb2i\xcb\x90\xca\x83 \xcb\x88e\xcb\x90\xc9\xbe\xca\xb2\xc9\x99n\xcc\xaa\xcb\xa0]</a></span>&#32;<span class="nowrap" style="font-size:85%">(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:Radio_Telef%C3%ADs_%C3%89ireann.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" decoding="async" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20" /></a></span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/8/84/Radio_Telef%C3%ADs_%C3%89ireann.ogg" class="internal" title="Radio Telef\xc3\xads \xc3\x89ireann.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</span>; <a href="/wiki/Irish_language" title="Irish language">Irish</a> for <i>Radio Television Ireland</i>) is an Irish <a href="/wiki/State-sponsored_bodies_of_the_Republic_of_Ireland" title="State-sponsored bodies of the Republic of Ireland">semi-state company</a> and <a href="/wiki/Public_broadcasting" title="Public broadcasting">public service broadcaster</a> headquartered in <a href="/wiki/Dublin" title="Dublin">Dublin</a>. It both produces programmes and broadcasts them on <a href="/wiki/RT%C3%89_Television" title="RT\xc3\x89 Television">television</a>, <a href="/wiki/RT%C3%89_Radio" title="RT\xc3\x89 Radio">radio</a> and <a href="/wiki/RT%C3%89.ie" title="RT\xc3\x89.ie">online</a>. The radio service began on 1 January 1926,<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> while regular television broadcasts began on 31 December 1961,<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> making it one of the oldest continuously operating public service broadcasters in the world. RT\xc3\x89 also publishes a weekly listings and lifestyle magazine, the <i><a href="/wiki/RT%C3%89_Guide" title="RT\xc3\x89 Guide">RT\xc3\x89 Guide</a></i>.\n</p><p>RT\xc3\x89 is a statutory body, overseen by a board appointed by the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Ireland" title="Government of Ireland">Government of Ireland</a>, with general management in the hands of the <a href="/wiki/RT%C3%89_Executive_Board" title="RT\xc3\x89 Executive Board">Executive Board</a>, headed by the Director-General. RT\xc3\x89 is regulated by the <a href="/wiki/Broadcasting_Authority_of_Ireland" title="Broadcasting Authority of Ireland">Broadcasting Authority of Ireland</a>. RT\xc3\x89 is financed by <a href="/wiki/Television_licensing_in_the_Republic_of_Ireland" title="Television licensing in the Republic of Ireland">television licence fee</a> and through <a href="/wiki/Advertising" title="Advertising">advertising</a>, with some of its services funded solely by advertising, while others are funded solely by the licence fee.\n</p><p>Radio \xc3\x89ireann, RT\xc3\x89\'s predecessor and at the time a section of the <a href="/wiki/Minister_for_Posts_and_Telegraphs" title="Minister for Posts and Telegraphs">Department of Posts and Telegraphs</a>, was one of 23 founding organisations of the <a href="/wiki/European_Broadcasting_Union" title="European Broadcasting Union">European Broadcasting Union</a> in 1950.\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc" class="toctext">Orchestras Quartet &amp; Choirs</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-23"><a href="#Infrastructure"><span class="tocnumber">5.3</span> <span class="toctext">Infrastructure</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-24"><a href="#Saorview"><span class="tocnumber">5.3.1</span> <span class="toctext">Saorview</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-25"><a href="#Saorsat"><span class="tocnumber">5.3.2</span> <span class="toctext">Saorsat</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-26"><a href="#Library"><span class="tocnumber">5.4</span> <span class="toctext">Library</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-27"><a href="#Logo"><span class="tocnumber">5.5</span> <span class="toctext">Logo</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-28"><a href="#Controversies_involving_RT\xc3\x89"><span class="tocnumber">6</span> <span class="toctext">Controversies involving RT\xc3\x89</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-29"><a href="#Competition_cases"><span class="tocnumber">6.1</span> <span class="toctext">Competition cases</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-30"><a href="#Death_of_Gerry_Ryan"><span class="tocnumber">6.2</span> <span class="toctext">Death of Gerry Ryan</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-31"><a href="#Defamation_cases"><span class="tocnumber">6.3</span> <span class="toctext">Defamation cases</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-32"><a href="#Moral_controversies"><span class="tocnumber">6.4</span> <span class="toctext">Moral controversies</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-33"><a href="#Political_controversies"><span class="tocnumber">6.5</span> <span class="toctext">Political controversies</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-34"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-35"><a href="#Further_reading"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">Further reading</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-36"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-37"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Raidi%C3%B3_Teilif%C3%ADs_%C3%89ireann&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<dl><dd><i>This section deals with the history of RT\xc3\x89 as an organisation. For details on this history of the various services see the separate articles on those services. For the history of the broadcasting service prior to 1960, see <a href="/wiki/Minister_for_Posts_and_Telegraphs" title="Minister for Posts and Telegraphs">Minister for Posts and Telegraphs</a> and <a href="/wiki/RT%C3%89_Radio_1" title="RT\xc3\x89 Radio 1">RT\xc3\x89 Radio 1</a>.</i></dd></dl>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Establishment_and_name">Establishment and name</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Raidi%C3%B3_Teilif%C3%ADs_%C3%89ireann&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Establishment and name">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Montrose_Studios_Donnybrook_2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Montrose_Studios_Donnybrook_2.jpg/220px-Montrose_Studios_Donnybrook_2.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Montrose_Studios_Donnybrook_2.jpg/330px-Montrose_Studios_Donnybrook_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Montrose_Studios_Donnybrook_2.jpg/440px-Montrose_Studios_Donnybrook_2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="986" data-file-height="658" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Montrose_Studios_Donnybrook_2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>RT\xc3\x89 campus entrance in Donnybrook</div></div></div>\n<p>Broadcasting in Ireland began in 1926 with <a href="/wiki/2RN" title="2RN">2RN</a> in Dublin. From that date until June 1960 the broadcasting service (2RN, later Radio \xc3\x89ireann) operated as a section of the Department of Posts and Telegraphs, and those working for the service were directly employed by the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Ireland" title="Government of Ireland">Irish Government</a> and regarded as <a href="/wiki/Civil_service_of_the_Republic_of_Ireland" class="mw-redirect" title="Civil service of the Republic of Ireland">civil servants</a>.\n</p><p>RT\xc3\x89 was established on 1 June 1960 (as <i>Radio \xc3\x89ireann</i>) under the Broadcasting Authority Act 1960, the principal legislation under which it still operates. The existing Radio \xc3\x89ireann service was transferred to the new authority, which was also made responsible for the new television service (<i>Telef\xc3\xads \xc3\x89ireann</i>). The television service started broadcasting on 31 December 1961, from the <a href="/wiki/Kippure" title="Kippure">Kippure</a> transmitter site near <a href="/wiki/Dublin" title="Dublin">Dublin</a>. <a href="/wiki/Eamonn_Andrews" title="Eamonn Andrews">Eamonn Andrews</a> was the first Chairman of Radio \xc3\x89ireann, the first director-general was Edward Roth. The name of the authority was changed, at the suggestion of <a href="/wiki/%C3%81ine_N%C3%AD_Cheanainn" title="\xc3\x81ine N\xc3\xad Cheanainn">\xc3\x81ine N\xc3\xad Cheanainn</a>, to <i>Radio Telef\xc3\xads \xc3\x89ireann</i><sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> by the Broadcasting Authority (Amendment) Act 1966, and both the radio and television services became known as RT\xc3\x89 in that year.\n</p><p>Section 113 of the Broadcasting Act 2009 changed the name of the organisation from "Radio Telef\xc3\xads \xc3\x89ireann" to "<a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/raidi%C3%B3" class="extiw" title="wikt:raidi\xc3\xb3">Raidi\xc3\xb3</a> Teilif\xc3\xads \xc3\x89ireann", to reflect the current standard spelling of the name in Irish.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> The spelling "Radio Telef\xc3\xads \xc3\x89ireann" remains carved in stone at the entrance to its headquarters in Dublin, Donnybrook.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Broadcasting_ban">Broadcasting ban</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Raidi%C3%B3_Teilif%C3%ADs_%C3%89ireann&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Broadcasting ban">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Under Section 31 of the Broadcasting Authority Act 1960 the Minister for Posts and Telegraphs of the day could direct RT\xc3\x89 "not to broadcast any matter, or any matter of any particular class".<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> In 1971 the first such directive was issued by <a href="/wiki/Gerry_Collins_(politician)" title="Gerry Collins (politician)">Gerry Collins</a>, directing RT\xc3\x89 not to broadcast "any matter that could be calculated to promote the aims or activities of any organisation which engages in, promotes, encourages or advocates the attaining of any particular objective by violent means".<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> A year later Collins dismissed the entire RT\xc3\x89 Authority over a report of an interview with <a href="/wiki/Se%C3%A1n_Mac_St%C3%ADof%C3%A1in" title="Se\xc3\xa1n Mac St\xc3\xadof\xc3\xa1in">Se\xc3\xa1n Mac St\xc3\xadof\xc3\xa1in</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Chief_of_Staff_of_the_Irish_Republican_Army" title="Chief of Staff of the Irish Republican Army">chief of staff</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Provisional_Irish_Republican_Army" title="Provisional Irish Republican Army">Provisional IRA</a>. RT\xc3\x89 reporter Kevin O\'Kelly had reported, not broadcast, his taped interview with Mac Stiof\xc3\xa1in. He was jailed briefly for contempt in a court case arising out of the interview, when Mac Stiof\xc3\xa1in was charged with IRA membership. O\'Kelly refused to identify Mac Stiof\xc3\xa1in\'s as the voice on his unbroadcast interview. The tape had been seized from his house by the <a href="/wiki/Garda_S%C3%ADoch%C3%A1na" title="Garda S\xc3\xadoch\xc3\xa1na">Garda S\xc3\xadoch\xc3\xa1na</a> (police).\n</p><p>In 1976, Section 31 was amended by <a href="/wiki/Conor_Cruise_O%27Brien" title="Conor Cruise O&#39;Brien">Conor Cruise O\'Brien</a> as 1973-77 Minister for Posts &amp; Telegraphs. He issued a new annually-based directive to the RT\xc3\x89 authority, prohibiting the broadcast of interviews or reports of interviews with spokespersons for, or representatives of, <a href="/wiki/Sinn_F%C3%A9in" title="Sinn F\xc3\xa9in">Sinn F\xc3\xa9in</a>, the IRA and other named organisations.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> RT\xc3\x89 was also banned from broadcasting interviews or reports of interviews with spokespersons for any organisation banned in Northern Ireland under the UK\'s <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland_(Emergency_Provisions)_Act_1973" title="Northern Ireland (Emergency Provisions) Act 1973">Northern Ireland (Emergency Provisions) Act 1973</a>. The directives were reissued on an annual basis, up to January 1993.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>During the late 1970s, RT\xc3\x89 was accused of extending the censorship rules into a system of self-censorship. A small minority of programme-makers also emerged who approved of Section 31, particularly supporters of the <a href="/wiki/Workers%27_Party_of_Ireland" title="Workers&#39; Party of Ireland">Workers\' Party</a> (formerly Sinn F\xc3\xa9in the Workers\' Party), including <a href="/wiki/Eoghan_Harris" title="Eoghan Harris">Eoghan Harris</a>, and Gerry Gregg who opposed that party\'s official policy. Opponents of censorship were portrayed as secret IRA sympathizers, including then reporter, later Irish President, Mary McAleese. She described the experience as, "the most difficult, the darkest, the worst time of my life".<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The effect of the Section 31 ban was more severe than the <a href="/wiki/1988%E2%80%931994_British_broadcasting_voice_restrictions" title="1988\xe2\x80\x931994 British broadcasting voice restrictions">censorship provision introduced in 1988</a> in the United Kingdom. The UK ban prevented direct speech of censored individuals. Broadcasters then used actors\' voices dubbing the recorded speech of censored persons. This was not permissible on RT\xc3\x89, which was prevented from broadcasting \'reports\' of interviews. British broadcasters interpreted the term \'spokesperson\' more loosely than RT\xc3\x89, that banned all Sinn F\xc3\xa9in members whether or not they were speaking on behalf of the party. The BBC interviewed Sinn F\xc3\xa9in President Gerry Adams as MP for West Belfast on 1 October 1990, speaking on unemployment in his constituency. Larry O\'Toole, then an ordinary Sinn F\xc3\xa9in member, mentioned this in a letter to RT\xc3\x89 Director of News Joe Mulhollend on 30 October 1990, after O\'Toole was banned by RT\xc3\x89 as spokesperson for striking bakery workers. O\'Toole then challenged the RTE ban in the High Court.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> In 1992\xe2\x80\x9393, in <i>O\'Toole vs RT\xc3\x89</i>, RT\xc3\x89 was found by the <a href="/wiki/High_Court_(Ireland)" title="High Court (Ireland)">High Court</a> and <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_Ireland" title="Supreme Court of Ireland">Supreme Court</a> to have illegally and unconstitutionally extended the censorship ban to Sinn F\xc3\xa9in members who were not speaking on behalf of Sinn F\xc3\xa9in. The RT\xc3\x89 ban did not affect UK stations broadcasting in the Republic of Ireland as, until 1988 at least, viewers in the Republic were still able to hear the voices of Sinn F\xc3\xa9in representatives.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="21st_century">21st century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Raidi%C3%B3_Teilif%C3%ADs_%C3%89ireann&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 21st century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In 2004, RT\xc3\x89 and the <a href="/wiki/Department_of_the_Environment,_Climate_and_Communications" title="Department of the Environment, Climate and Communications">Minister for Communications, Marine and Natural Resources</a> agreed that in future, RT\xc3\x89 would operate under a Public Service Broadcasting Charter.\n</p><p>On 29 June 2005 the Minister appointed the members of a new RT\xc3\x89 Authority, replacing the previous one appointed in June 2000. Fintan Drury, chairman of Platinum sports management, and also chairman of <a href="/wiki/Paddy_Power" title="Paddy Power">Paddy Power</a> plc, was appointed chairman of RT\xc3\x89. The other members of the Authority are Maria Killian, Patricia King, Ian Malcolm, Patrick Marron, Una N\xc3\xad Chonaire, Emer Finnan, Stephen O\'Byrnes and Joe O\'Brien. The new Authority would hold office for not more than three years. On 11 January 2006, Fintan Drury resigned as chairman of RT\xc3\x89, citing a potential conflict of interest in his role as an advisor to the organisers of the <a href="/wiki/Ryder_Cup" title="Ryder Cup">Ryder Cup</a> golf tournament and as chairman of a broadcaster involved in a row over broadcasting rights. This occurred after Irish government proposals to add the tournament to the list of sports events which must be broadcast on free-to-air terrestrial television, to which <a href="/wiki/British_Sky_Broadcasting" class="mw-redirect" title="British Sky Broadcasting">British Sky Broadcasting</a>, the rights holders, were objecting. On 22 February 2006, Mary Finan was appointed Chairperson<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> of the RT\xc3\x89 Authority.\n</p><p>In September 2006, the Government published the proposed text of the <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20061109062100/http://www.econsultation.ie/">Broadcasting Bill 2006</a>. It proposed that RT\xc3\x89 and TG4 would become separate <a href="/wiki/Company_Limited_by_Guarantee" class="mw-redirect" title="Company Limited by Guarantee">companies limited by guarantee</a>, with the Minister as sole member of both companies (CLGs do not have shareholders). RT\xc3\x89 would be legally obliged to agree a charter every five years and publish a statement of commitments every year, and be under the jurisdiction of the proposed <a href="/wiki/Broadcasting_Authority_of_Ireland" title="Broadcasting Authority of Ireland">Broadcasting Authority of Ireland</a>. The bill was delayed, but was finally introduced into D\xc3\xa1il \xc3\x89ireann on 14 April 2008. The Broadcasting Act 2009<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> retains RT\xc3\x89 as a statutory corporation, but renamed the RT\xc3\x89 Authority as the RT\xc3\x89 Board and made changes to the way it is appointed. It also renamed the corporation <i>Raidi\xc3\xb3 Teilif\xc3\xads \xc3\x89ireann</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> with the <i><a href="/wiki/Irish_Times" class="mw-redirect" title="Irish Times">Irish Times</a></i> noting that this thereby fixed a "spelling error that lasted 40 years". In the meantime, the <i>Broadcasting (Amendment) Act 2007</i> awarded RT\xc3\x89 control of one multiplex for <a href="/wiki/Digital_terrestrial_television" title="Digital terrestrial television">digital terrestrial television</a> and giving it responsibilities in relation to broadcasting outside the state. In line with this, RT\xc3\x89 and the government were currently in discussions with regard to a new channel proposed for to launch outside the Republic, which initially had the working titles of <i>Diaspora TV</i>, and later <a href="/wiki/RT%C3%89_International" class="mw-redirect" title="RT\xc3\x89 International">RT\xc3\x89 International</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> In April 2007, <a href="/wiki/TG4" title="TG4">TG4</a> became an independent statutory corporation, having previously been a <a href="/wiki/Wholly_owned_subsidiary" class="mw-redirect" title="Wholly owned subsidiary">wholly owned subsidiary</a> of RT\xc3\x89 since its inception. RT\xc3\x89 continues to contribute programmes to the channel, including <a href="/wiki/Nuacht_TG4" title="Nuacht TG4">Nuacht TG4</a>.\n</p><p>In July 2007, RT\xc3\x89 began participating in a HD trial in Dublin, showing programmes such as <a href="/wiki/Planet_Earth_(2006_TV_series)" title="Planet Earth (2006 TV series)">Planet Earth</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gaelic_Athletic_Association" title="Gaelic Athletic Association">Gaelic Athletic Association</a> matches. RT\xc3\x89 announced its plan to launch two further television channels; one general entertainment channel \xe2\x80\x93 <i><a href="/wiki/RT%C3%89_Three" title="RT\xc3\x89 Three">RT\xc3\x89 Three</a></i> (working name) \xe2\x80\x93 and a timeshift service for <a href="/wiki/RT%C3%89_One" title="RT\xc3\x89 One">RT\xc3\x89 One</a> \xe2\x80\x93 <i>RT\xc3\x89 One +1</i> (working name).<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 24 February 2009 the Minister for Communications, Energy, and Natural Resources, appointed the members of a new RT\xc3\x89 Authority, replacing the previous one appointed in June 2006. <a href="/wiki/Tom_Savage_(Irish_media_figure)" title="Tom Savage (Irish media figure)">Tom Savage</a> of the Communications Clinic was appointed chairman of RT\xc3\x89. The other members of the Authority were Patricia Quinn, <a href="/wiki/Karlin_Lillington" title="Karlin Lillington">Karlin Lillington</a>, Fergus Armstrong, <a href="/wiki/Alan_Gilsenan" title="Alan Gilsenan">Alan Gilsenan</a>, Se\xc3\xa1n O\'Sullivan, Emer Finnan. Cathal Goan then Director General, RT\xc3\x89 as an ex-officio member of the Authority. The new Authority held office for not more than six months, due to changes planned under the <a href="/wiki/Broadcasting_Act_2009" title="Broadcasting Act 2009">Broadcasting Act 2009</a> which became law on 12 July 2009, dissolving the authority, and replacing it with an RT\xc3\x89 Board. Under Section 179 (3) of the Act, any person who was a member of the Authority when the Act was signed into law continues as a member of the Board until the end of their term of office on 24 August 2009. Unlike the RT\xc3\x89 Authority, the RT\xc3\x89 Board has not the self-regulatory function over RT\xc3\x89, as this was transferred to a newly appointed Broadcasting Authority of Ireland that replaces the <a href="/wiki/Broadcasting_Commission_of_Ireland" class="mw-redirect" title="Broadcasting Commission of Ireland">Broadcasting Commission of Ireland</a> regulating commercial TV and radio. This helps assuage any concerns of the potential for bias that could be perceived under previous self-regulation by having a single regulator of public service and commercial Irish broadcasters into the future.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 1 June 2009, the <i><a href="/wiki/Sunday_Independent_(Ireland)" title="Sunday Independent (Ireland)">Sunday Independent</a></i> reported that RT\xc3\x89 was on the brink of bankruptcy.<sup id="cite_ref-Belfast_Bankrupt_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Belfast_Bankrupt-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> Such reports are denied by RT\xc3\x89, though the organisation acknowledges how under the current financial structure there is "serious financial difficulty" and a review of its financial procedures is underway and to be completed by 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> On 11 June 2009 the Director General of RT\xc3\x89 <a href="/wiki/Cathal_Goan" title="Cathal Goan">Cathal Goan</a> reported to the <a href="/wiki/Oireachtas" title="Oireachtas">Oireachtas</a> that RT\xc3\x89 was not bankrupt and that it would break even by year end<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> On 3 July 2009, the RT\xc3\x89 2008 Annual Report was published. The organisation <a href="/wiki/Break-even" title="Break-even">broke even</a> in 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> On 29 September 2009, RT\xc3\x89 revealed a proposal for the regeneration of its existing building estimated to cost \xe2\x82\xac350&#160;million. If approved, the project would see the gradual replacement over a 10- to 15-year period of most of the current 1960s and 1970s buildings on the Donnybrook site. The new building would accommodate the switch over to high-definition, additional channels and new studios.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> RT\xc3\x89 has since received planning consent from Dublin City Council for an application for the redevelopment of the station\'s Donnybrook site.The proposal for redevelopment of the site was accepted by local councillors last November 2009.The next stage of the planning process involves all parties having an opportunity to lodge appeals with An Bord Plean\xc3\xa1la over the coming four weeks (by May 2010). The proposal would also involve building a new entrance onto the N11 Stillorgan dual carriageway.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Noel_Curran" title="Noel Curran">Noel Curran</a> was appointed <a href="/wiki/Director-General_of_RT%C3%89" title="Director-General of RT\xc3\x89">Director-General of RT\xc3\x89</a> from 1 February 2011 on 9 November 2010 for five years, replacing <a href="/wiki/Cathal_Goan" title="Cathal Goan">Cathal Goan</a> who had decided not to seek an extension to the seven-year term which ended at end of January 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-Department_of_Communications,_Energy_&amp;_Natural_Resources_Press_Releases_2010_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Department_of_Communications,_Energy_&amp;_Natural_Resources_Press_Releases_2010-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> It was announced on 1 April 2016 that <a href="/wiki/Dee_Forbes" title="Dee Forbes">Dee Forbes</a> would be the new Director General.<sup id="cite_ref-RT\xc3\x89_appoints_Dee_Forbes_as_new_Director_General_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RT\xc3\x89_appoints_Dee_Forbes_as_new_Director_General-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2012, RT\xc3\x89 broadcast advertisements on <a href="/wiki/Christmas_Day" class="mw-redirect" title="Christmas Day">Christmas Day</a> in a break with tradition.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Income_and_expenditure">Income and expenditure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Raidi%C3%B3_Teilif%C3%ADs_%C3%89ireann&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Income and expenditure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Attribution_of_licence_fee_by_RT%C3%89_Ireland_2008.png" class="image"><img alt="Attribution of licence fee by RT\xc3\x89 Ireland 2008.png" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Attribution_of_licence_fee_by_RT%C3%89_Ireland_2008.png/220px-Attribution_of_licence_fee_by_RT%C3%89_Ireland_2008.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="170" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Attribution_of_licence_fee_by_RT%C3%89_Ireland_2008.png/330px-Attribution_of_licence_fee_by_RT%C3%89_Ireland_2008.png 1.5x, class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div></div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Budget">Budget</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Raidi%C3%B3_Teilif%C3%ADs_%C3%89ireann&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Budget">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The following figures were issued by RT\xc3\x89 as part of their annual report in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> In 2012 RT\xc3\x89 received in total \xe2\x82\xac180,894,000 in public funding from the licence fee, it also received \xe2\x82\xac127,100,000 in commercial revenue. RT\xc3\x89 total expenditure in 2012 was \xe2\x82\xac327,023,000. They had restructuring costs of \xe2\x82\xac46,161,000 in 2012. Losses for the year came to \xe2\x82\xac65,147,000.\n</p><p>Profit and Loss across radio, television and online services.\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th>Income Type\n</th>\n<th>RT\xc3\x89 One\n</th>\n<th>RT\xc3\x89 Two\n</th>\n<th>RT\xc3\x89 Television\n</th>\n<th>Radio 1\n</th>\n<th>2fm\n</th>\n<th>Lyric FM\n</th>\n<th>RnaG\n</th>\n<th>Total Radio\n</th>\n<th>RT\xc3\x89 Performing Groups\n</th>\n<th>RT\xc3\x89.ie\n</th>\n<th>DTT Costs\n</th>\n<th>Other Channels\n</th>\n<th>TG4 Support\n</th>\n<th>\n</th>\n<th>Totals\n</th></tr>\n<tr style="text-align:center; Within the State, it is necessary to pay a fee of \xe2\x82\xac160 <i>per annum</i> to legally possess any piece of equipment capable of receiving television signals (not necessarily those of RT\xc3\x89). This money is collected by <a href="/wiki/An_Post" title="An Post">An Post</a> on behalf of the <a href="/wiki/Minister_for_Tourism,_Culture,_Arts,_Gaeltacht,_Sport_and_Media" title="Minister for Tourism, Culture, Arts, Gaeltacht, Sport and Media">Minister for Tourism, Culture, Arts, Gaeltacht, Sport and Media</a>. The state pays for TV Licence Inspectors who have the power to obtain and execute search warrants of private houses. Failure to possess a valid television licence can result in a fine and a criminal record.</li>\n<li>Commercial revenue including the sale of advertising and <a href="/wiki/Sponsor_(commercial)" title="Sponsor (commercial)">sponsorship</a>. In the early 1990s Minister <a href="/wiki/Ray_Burke_(Irish_politician)" title="Ray Burke (Irish politician)">Ray Burke</a> imposed commercial revenue quotas to limit the amount of revenue that RT\xc3\x89 could procure through advertising, in view of the corporation\'s licence fee income. While such quotas were later removed RT\xc3\x89 Radio and Television is still limited to 6 minutes of advertising per hour<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>. The commercial division owned 0.086% of the <a href="/wiki/Intelsat" title="Intelsat">Intelsat</a> satellite firm, which it sold in 2005.</li></ul>\n<p>Even though commercial quotas have been removed, commercial revenue and the license fee each contribute roughly half of the organization\'s income. The licence fee does not fund <a href="/wiki/RT%C3%89_2fm" title="RT\xc3\x89 2fm">RT\xc3\x89 2fm</a>, <a href="/wiki/RT%C3%89_Aertel" title="RT\xc3\x89 Aertel">RT\xc3\x89 Aertel</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/RT%C3%89_Guide" title="RT\xc3\x89 Guide">RT\xc3\x89 Guide</a></i> or the website <a href="/wiki/RT%C3%89.ie" title="RT\xc3\x89.ie">RT\xc3\x89.ie</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-RT\xc3\x89_Annual_Report_2009_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RT\xc3\x89_Annual_Report_2009-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> however, each of these brands are indirectly funded by the licence fee through the use of content that is funded by the licence fee, such as News and Current Affairs.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Breakdown_of_the_licence_fee">Breakdown of the licence fee</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Raidi%C3%B3_Teilif%C3%ADs_%C3%89ireann&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7"
