Cost</b></td>\n<td><b>160.00</b></td>\n<td><b>160.00</b></td>\n<td><b>160.00</b>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h3><span id="RT.C3.89_personality_salaries"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="RT\xc3\x89_personality_salaries">RT\xc3\x89 personality salaries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Raidi%C3%B3_Teilif%C3%ADs_%C3%89ireann&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: RT\xc3\x89 personality salaries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>RT\xc3\x89\'s Director General in October 2009 said there was "no question that by today\'s standards" the salaries paid to its top presenters in 2008 "were excessive. I have to repeat that they were set at a different time in a different competitive reality where some of this talent might be up for poaching by other organisations and in RT\xc3\x89\'s view at the time, they delivered value for money ".<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Fine_Gael" title="Fine Gael">Fine Gael</a> said the high salaries were "rubbing salt in the wounds" for people who had lost their jobs or taken significant pay cuts. Labour criticised RT\xc3\x89 for not releasing the data sooner and said "This information should be easily available and there should be no question of concealing it or making it in any way inaccessible ".<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> Many of the highest-paid stars are not technically members of staff but are paid through separate companies, enabling them and the station to avoid paying tax on their salaries.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In December 2018, RT\xc3\x89 published the list of salaries paid to its top 10 personalities in 2016:\n</p>\n<ol><li><a href="/wiki/Ryan_Tubridy" title="Ryan Tubridy">Ryan Tubridy</a>: \xe2\x82\xac495,000</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Ray_D%27Arcy" title="Ray D&#39;Arcy">Ray D\'Arcy</a>: \xe2\x82\xac450,000</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Joe_Duffy" title="Joe Duffy">Joe Duffy</a>: \xe2\x82\xac389,988</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Sean_O%27Rourke" title="Sean O&#39;Rourke">Sean O\'Rourke</a>: \xe2\x82\xac308,964</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Marian_Finucane" title="Marian Finucane">Marian Finucane</a>: \xe2\x82\xac300,617</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Miriam_O%27Callaghan" title="Miriam O&#39;Callaghan">Miriam O\'Callaghan</a>: \xe2\x82\xac299,000</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Claire_Byrne" title="Claire Byrne">Claire Byrne</a>: \xe2\x82\xac216,000</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Bryan_Dobson" title="Bryan Dobson">Bryan Dobson</a>: \xe2\x82\xac198,146</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/George_Hamilton_(broadcaster)" title="George Hamilton (broadcaster)">George Hamilton</a>: \xe2\x82\xac186,195</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Mary_Wilson_(broadcaster)" title="Mary Wilson (broadcaster)">Mary Wilson</a>: \xe2\x82\xac185,679<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup></li></ol>\n<p>RT\xc3\x89 Director-General, Dee Forbes, said: \xe2\x80\x9cThe audited figures released today for 2016 sees RT\xc3\x89 maintain our commitment to reduce these earnings by 30% as compared to 2008 levels, while continuing to value the significant contribution our presenters make, and to RT\xc3\x89\xe2\x80\x99s ability to optimise commercial revenue to support Ireland\xe2\x80\x99s public media.\n</p><p>"This will continue to be an area of focus for me. Within a challenging marketplace and in the absence of meaningful funding reform, we are making significant efforts to reduce costs across the organisation, in addition to the considerable reduction in operating costs implemented since 2008.\xe2\x80\x9d<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Organisation">Organisation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Raidi%C3%B3_Teilif%C3%ADs_%C3%89ireann&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Organisation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/RT%C3%89_Authority" class="mw-redirect" title="RT\xc3\x89 Authority">RT\xc3\x89 Authority</a>, <a href="/wiki/RT%C3%89_Executive" class="mw-redirect" title="RT\xc3\x89 Executive">RT\xc3\x89 Executive</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Director-General_of_RT%C3%89" title="Director-General of RT\xc3\x89">Director-General of RT\xc3\x89</a></div>\n<h3><span id="RT.C3.89_Board_and_Executive_Board"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="RT\xc3\x89_Board_and_Executive_Board">RT\xc3\x89 Board and Executive Board</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Raidi%C3%B3_Teilif%C3%ADs_%C3%89ireann&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: RT\xc3\x89 Board and Executive Board">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>RT\xc3\x89 is a statutory corporation. Under its original governance arrangements (under the Broadcasting Authority Act 1960) its board was known as the RT\xc3\x89 Authority. The members of the RT\xc3\x89 Authority were appointed by the Cabinet upon the recommendation of the <a href="/wiki/Minister_for_the_Environment,_Climate_and_Communications" title="Minister for the Environment, Climate and Communications">Minister for Communications, Marine and Natural Resources</a>. The RT\xc3\x89 Authority was both the legal owner of RT\xc3\x89 (under the 1960 Act, it <i>was</i> RT\xc3\x89) and was also its regulator.\n</p><p>Under the <a href="/wiki/Broadcasting_Act_2009" title="Broadcasting Act 2009">Broadcasting Act 2009</a>, RT\xc3\x89\'s governance arrangements have changed. The statutory corporation form has been retained, but the new Act no longer refers to the board of RT\xc3\x89 as an "Authority" and it is now simply known as the Board. Of the 12 members of the Board which replaced the RT\xc3\x89 Authority, the Minister appoints six, the Oireachtas Committee on the Environment, Climate and Communications decides on four names to present to the Minister for appointment, one member is elected by the staff of RT\xc3\x89, and the Director General sits on the Board <i>ex officio</i>. The final members of the RT\xc3\x89 Authority were reappointed to the new Board in the interim.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> The provisions of the Act relating to the Broadcasting Authority of Ireland were commenced on 1 October 2009 (under <a href="/wiki/Statutory_Instrument" class="mw-redirect" title="Statutory Instrument">Statutory Instrument</a> 389 of 2009 of the <a href="/wiki/Broadcasting_Act_2009" title="Broadcasting Act 2009">Broadcasting Act 2009</a>), RT\xc3\x89 is externally regulated by the <a href="/wiki/Broadcasting_Authority_of_Ireland" title="Broadcasting Authority of Ireland">Broadcasting Authority of Ireland</a>.\n</p><p>The RT\xc3\x89 organisation is divided into six integrated business divisions (termed "IBDs" within RT\xc3\x89): <a href="/wiki/RT%C3%89_Television" title="RT\xc3\x89 Television">RT\xc3\x89 Television</a>, <a href="/wiki/RT%C3%89_Radio" title="RT\xc3\x89 Radio">RT\xc3\x89 Radio</a>, <a href="/wiki/RT%C3%89_News_and_Current_Affairs" title="RT\xc3\x89 News and Current Affairs">RT\xc3\x89 News and Current Affairs</a>, <a href="/wiki/2RN_(RT%C3%89_Networks)" title="2RN (RT\xc3\x89 Networks)">RT\xc3\x89 Network</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=RT%C3%89_Digital&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="RT\xc3\x89 Digital (page does not exist)">RT\xc3\x89 Digital</a> and <a href="/wiki/RT%C3%89_Performing_Groups" title="RT\xc3\x89 Performing Groups">RT\xc3\x89 Orchestras Quartet &amp; Choirs</a>, together with Centrally Incurred Shared Services (Group Communications, Legal &amp; Treasury, Central HR &amp; IT Support, Group Insurance &amp; Pension, Property and Site Facilities, <i>RT\xc3\x89 Guide</i> Production, Publication &amp; Advertising Sales) and a Corporate Headquarters. The Irish-language channel, <a href="/wiki/TG4" title="TG4">TG4</a>, was operated as a subsidiary of RT\xc3\x89 (Serbhis\xc3\xad Telef\xc3\xads na Gaeilge Teoranta) prior to its separation from RT\xc3\x89 on 1 April 2007.\n</p><p>The RT\xc3\x89 Board appoints the <a href="/wiki/Director-General_of_RT%C3%89" title="Director-General of RT\xc3\x89">Director-General of RT\xc3\x89</a> who in effect fulfils the dual role of chief executive and of Editor in Chief. The Director-General heads the Executive Board of RT\xc3\x89, which comprises the company\'s top management and includes the chief financial officer, the Director of Communications and the Managing Directors of the Television, Radio, and News divisions.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Broadcasting">Broadcasting</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Raidi%C3%B3_Teilif%C3%ADs_%C3%89ireann&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Broadcasting">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Radio">Radio</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Raidi%C3%B3_Teilif%C3%ADs_%C3%89ireann&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Radio">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/RT%C3%89_Radio" title="RT\xc3\x89 Radio">RT\xc3\x89 Radio</a></div>\n<p>The first voice broadcast of <a href="/wiki/2RN" title="2RN">2RN</a>, the original radio <a href="/wiki/Callsign" class="mw-redirect" title="Callsign">callsign</a> for Radio 1, took place on 14 November 1925 when Seamus Clandillon, the 2RN station director said, \'Seo Raidi\xc3\xb3 2RN, Baile \xc3\x81tha Cliath ag t\xc3\xa1st\xc3\xa1il\', Irish for \'This is Radio 2RN, Dublin calling\'. Regular Irish radio-broadcasting began on 1 January 1926. Unfortunately, most Irish people could not receive 2RN\'s (1.5 kilowatt) signal. When faced with numerous complaints from Cork regarding the writers\' inability to tune to the signal, Clandillon remarked in <i>The Irish Radio Review</i>, a magazine dedicated to the service, that they did not know how to operate their sets. 6CK was established in <a href="/wiki/Cork_(city)" title="Cork (city)">Cork</a> in 1927; much of 6CK\'s output was simply a relay of the national service but it also had a significant input into the programmes of 2RN until it was closed down in the 1950s.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Montrose_Studios_Donnybrook.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Montrose_Studios_Donnybrook.jpg/220px-Montrose_Studios_Donnybrook.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="330" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Montrose_Studios_Donnybrook.jpg/330px-Montrose_Studios_Donnybrook.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Montrose_Studios_Donnybrook.jpg/440px-Montrose_Studios_Donnybrook.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1760" data-file-height="2640" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Montrose_Studios_Donnybrook.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>RT\xc3\x89 links mast at <a href="/wiki/Donnybrook,_Dublin" title="Donnybrook, Dublin">Donnybrook</a> campus</div></div></div>\n<p>A high-power (initially 60&#160;kW) station was established in <a href="/wiki/Athlone" title="Athlone">Athlone</a>, in 1932, to coincide with the staging of the <a href="/wiki/Eucharistic_Congress" class="mw-redirect" title="Eucharistic Congress">Eucharistic Congress</a>. 2RN, 6CK and Athlone became known as "Radio Athlone" (Irish: <i lang="ga">Raidi\xc3\xb3 \xc3\x81th Luain</i>) and were receivable across virtually the entire country. Radio Athlone became known as "Radio \xc3\x89ireann" in 1938.\n</p><p>Radio \xc3\x89ireann tried to satisfy all tastes on a single channel (with very limited programming hours). However, this resulted in a rather conservative programming policy. It was barely tolerated by most Irish listeners, and usually trounced (particularly on the east coast and along the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland" title="Northern Ireland">Northern Ireland</a> border) by the <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a> and later <a href="/wiki/Radio_Luxembourg_(English)" class="mw-redirect" title="Radio Luxembourg (English)">Radio Luxembourg</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> This did not really change until Radio \xc3\x89ireann became free of direct government control in the 1960s.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (December 2013)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup><br />\nIn 1973 the radio service moved from the GPO in the centre of Dublin, where it had been housed since 1928, into a new purpose-built <a href="/wiki/RT%C3%89_Radio_Centre" title="RT\xc3\x89 Radio Centre">Radio Centre</a> beside the existing <a href="/wiki/RT%C3%89_Television_Centre" title="RT\xc3\x89 Television Centre">Television Centre</a> on the Donnybrook campus.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:RT%C3%89_clock.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/RT%C3%89_clock.jpg/220px-RT%C3%89_clock.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/RT%C3%89_clock.jpg/330px-RT%C3%89_clock.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/RT%C3%89_clock.jpg/440px-RT%C3%89_clock.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="4000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:RT%C3%89_clock.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Clock at RT\xc3\x89 buildings, <a href="/wiki/Cork_(city)" title="Cork (city)">Cork</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Now, RT\xc3\x89 has a nationwide communications network with an increasing emphasis on regional news-gathering and input. Broadcasting on <a href="/wiki/RT%C3%89_Radio_1" title="RT\xc3\x89 Radio 1">Radio 1</a> provides comprehensive coverage of news, current affairs, music, drama and variety features, agriculture, education, religion and sport, mostly in English but also some Irish. <a href="/wiki/RT%C3%89_2fm" title="RT\xc3\x89 2fm">RT\xc3\x89 2fm</a> is a popular music and chat channel which commenced broadcasting as RT\xc3\x89 Radio 2 on 31 May 1979, Brendan Balfe being the first voice to be heard on the station at midday when he introduced the first presenter, Larry Gogan. <a href="/wiki/RT%C3%89_lyric_fm" title="RT\xc3\x89 lyric fm">RT\xc3\x89 lyric fm</a> serves the interests of classical music and the arts, coming on air in May 1999, and replacing FM3 Classical Music, which had catered for the same target audience and time-shared with <a href="/wiki/RT%C3%89_Raidi%C3%B3_na_Gaeltachta" title="RT\xc3\x89 Raidi\xc3\xb3 na Gaeltachta">RT\xc3\x89 Raidi\xc3\xb3 na Gaeltachta</a>, an exclusively Irish language service, which first began broadcasting on Easter Sunday, 2 April 1972.\nFormerly RT\xc3\x89 operated <a href="/wiki/RT%C3%89_Radio_Cork" title="RT\xc3\x89 Radio Cork">RT\xc3\x89 Radio Cork</a> (previously \'Cork 89FM\' and \'RT\xc3\x89 Cork Local Radio\'), a local radio service in Cork, but this closed down in 2000.\n</p><p>A slightly adapted version of Radio 1 is broadcast as RT\xc3\x89 Europe on <a href="/wiki/Eurobird" title="Eurobird">Eurobird</a>; the main difference between this and the main FM feed is the inclusion of several programmes taken from RT\xc3\x89 Radio na Gaeltachta.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Digital_audio_broadcasting" title="Digital audio broadcasting">DAB</a> test broadcasts of RT\xc3\x89\'s four stations began on 1 January 2006, along the east coast of Ireland, also carrying the private <a href="/wiki/Today_FM" title="Today FM">Today FM</a> and <a href="/wiki/WRN_Broadcast" title="WRN Broadcast">World Radio Network</a>, to which RT\xc3\x89 is a contributing broadcaster. DAB was launched to the public in late 2006, and now contains six RT\xc3\x89 digital-only stations&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 <a href="/wiki/RT%C3%89_2XM" title="RT\xc3\x89 2XM">RT\xc3\x89 2XM</a>, <a href="/wiki/RT%C3%89_Chill" title="RT\xc3\x89 Chill">RT\xc3\x89 Chill</a>, <a href="/wiki/RT%C3%89_Gold" title="RT\xc3\x89 Gold">RT\xc3\x89 Gold</a>, <a href="/wiki/RT%C3%89_Junior" class="mw-redirect" title="RT\xc3\x89 Junior">RT\xc3\x89 Junior</a>, <a href="/wiki/RT%C3%89_Pulse" title="RT\xc3\x89 Pulse">RT\xc3\x89 Pulse</a> and <a href="/wiki/RT%C3%89_Radio_1_Extra" title="RT\xc3\x89 Radio 1 Extra">RT\xc3\x89 Radio 1 Extra</a>&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 as well as the four terrestrial services. There were also two other DAB Services, <a href="/wiki/RT%C3%89_Digital_Radio_News" title="RT\xc3\x89 Digital Radio News">RT\xc3\x89 Digital Radio News</a> and <a href="/wiki/RT%C3%89_Choice" title="RT\xc3\x89 Choice">RT\xc3\x89 Choice</a>, both of which have been shut down. RT\xc3\x89\'s radio stations are also carried on digital cable and satellite platforms in Ireland, as well as on <a href="/wiki/Digital_terrestrial_television" title="Digital terrestrial television">digital terrestrial television</a>, and RT\xc3\x89 Radio 1 has been carried on shortwave in <a href="/wiki/Digital_Radio_Mondiale" title="Digital Radio Mondiale">DRM</a> during specific events, including the <a href="/wiki/All_Ireland" class="mw-redirect" title="All Ireland">All Ireland</a> finals.\n</p><p>A survey carried out by the Department of Community, Rural and Gaeltacht Affairs showed that demand for an Irish-language radio station aimed at a younger audience than <a href="/wiki/RT%C3%89_Raidi%C3%B3_na_Gaeltachta" title="RT\xc3\x89 Raidi\xc3\xb3 na Gaeltachta">RT\xc3\x89 Raidi\xc3\xb3 na Gaeltachta</a> was high. This means that RT\xc3\x89 might have plans to launch such a radio station.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In August 2009, faced with falling audience listening figures, a media analyst, David Quinn, organiser of the religiously-motivated "Iona Institute" pressure group, advised that RT\xc3\x89 has "alienated some of the audience it ought to be going after" and should "try to be more even-handed in its treatment of the issues of the day instead of pushing every PC cause going."<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>With the closure of Saor Raidi\xc3\xb3 Chonamara ("Free Radio Connemara"), it showed the importance and it showed awareness for the Irish language. With this in mind, it forced RT\xc3\x89 to agree to join with Raidi\xc3\xb3 na Gaeltachta, which is still present today.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Television">Television</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Raidi%C3%B3_Teilif%C3%ADs_%C3%89ireann&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Television">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/RT%C3%89_Television" title="RT\xc3\x89 Television">RT\xc3\x89 Television</a></div>\n<p>In the Republic of Ireland, <a href="/wiki/RT%C3%89_One" title="RT\xc3\x89 One">RT\xc3\x89 One</a> and <a href="/wiki/RT%C3%892" title="RT\xc3\x892">RT\xc3\x892</a> are RT\xc3\x89\'s flagship channels and are broadcast on <a href="/wiki/Saorview" title="Saorview">Saorview</a> (Ireland\'s digital television system) along with, <a href="/wiki/RT%C3%89_News_Now" class="mw-redirect" title="RT\xc3\x89 News Now">RT\xc3\x89 News Now</a>, <a href="/wiki/RT%C3%89jr" title="RT\xc3\x89jr">RT\xc3\x89jr</a> and timeshift services, RT\xc3\x89 One +1, and RT\xc3\x892+1. RT\xc3\x89 Television also offers two further services: RT\xc3\x89 Live, where viewers can watch RT\xc3\x89 as it broadcasts live on the internet, using programming from both RT\xc3\x89 One and RT\xc3\x892 and <a href="/wiki/RT%C3%89_Player" title="RT\xc3\x89 Player">RT\xc3\x89 Player</a> an on-demand video service. Both of these services are available on a national and international basis.\n</p>\n<ul><li><b>Timeline</b></li></ul>\n<dl><dt>1920s</dt>\n<dd></dd></dl>\n<p>Ireland was one of the first countries in Europe to embrace the medium of radio, but was a relative latecomer to television. Unlike its European counterparts, the Government of Ireland did not use the medium of television until 31 December 1961. Countries such as the United Kingdom (1929), France (1935) and Italy (1954) embraced television long before Ireland. Prior to the launch of the Republic of Ireland\'s national broadcaster RT\xc3\x89, television services were available, though limited, from Northern Ireland through <a href="/wiki/BBC_Northern_Ireland" title="BBC Northern Ireland">BBC Northern Ireland</a> (1955) and <a href="/wiki/UTV_(TV_channel)" title="UTV (TV channel)">UTV</a> (1959) . The development of the <a href="/wiki/Divis_transmitting_station" title="Divis transmitting station">Divis</a> transmitter in Northern Ireland in July 1955 allowed overspill of these services into the Republic.\n</p>\n<dl><dt>1950s</dt>\n<dd></dd></dl>\n<p>In the late 1950s, a <i>Television Committee</i> was formed; its goal was to set up an Irish television service with as little financial support from the government.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> It initially recommended setting up a service along the lines of <a href="/wiki/ITV_(TV_network)" title="ITV (TV network)">ITV</a>, using five mountain tops as transmission sites, which were also equipped for <a href="/wiki/FM_radio" class="mw-redirect" title="FM radio">FM radio</a> transmission. However, since <a href="/wiki/%C3%89amon_de_Valera" title="\xc3\x89amon de Valera">\xc3\x89amon de Valera</a> was somewhat wary of television, nothing more of consequence was done until <a href="/wiki/Se%C3%A1n_Lemass" title="Se\xc3\xa1n Lemass">Se\xc3\xa1n Lemass</a> succeeded him as <a href="/wiki/Taoiseach" title="Taoiseach">Taoiseach</a> in 1959. A year later, Radio \xc3\x89ireann was converted from an arm of the <a href="/wiki/Minister_for_Posts_and_Telegraphs" title="Minister for Posts and Telegraphs">Department of Posts and Telegraphs</a> into a <a href="/wiki/State-sponsored_bodies_of_the_Republic_of_Ireland" title="State-sponsored bodies of the Republic of Ireland">semi-state body</a> and given responsibility for television. <a href="/wiki/Eamonn_Andrews" title="Eamonn Andrews">Eamonn Andrews</a> was appointed as the new chairman. A site for a new <a href="/wiki/RT%C3%89_Television_Centre" title="RT\xc3\x89 Television Centre">Television Production Centre</a> had been found in 1959, and its construction started in October 1960.\n</p>\n<dl><dt>1960s</dt>\n<dd></dd></dl>\n<p>Telef\xc3\xads \xc3\x89ireann began broadcasting at 19:00 on New Year\'s Eve, 1961. The channel was launched with opening address by the then <a href="/wiki/President_of_Ireland" title="President of Ireland">President de Valera</a>. There were other messages from <a href="/wiki/John_D%27Alton" title="John D&#39;Alton">Cardinal d\'Alton</a> and Lemass; following this, a live concert was broadcast from the Gresham Hotel in <a href="/wiki/Dublin" title="Dublin">Dublin</a>. The show, which was a countdown to the New Year, was hosted by Andrews, with appearances by tenor Patrick O\'Hagan (father of <a href="/wiki/Johnny_Logan_(singer)" title="Johnny Logan (singer)">Johnny Logan</a>), the <a href="/wiki/Artane,_Dublin#Artane_Band" title="Artane, Dublin">Artane Boys\' Band</a> and <a href="/wiki/Michael_O%27Hehir" title="Michael O&#39;Hehir">Michael O\'Hehir</a>. Television became an important force within Irish culture as it helped to explore topics often deemed controversial such as <a href="/wiki/Abortion_in_the_Republic_of_Ireland" title="Abortion in the Republic of Ireland">abortion</a> and contraception. The development of entertainment show <i><a href="/wiki/The_Late_Late_Show_(Ireland)" class="mw-redirect" title="The Late Late Show (Ireland)">The Late Late Show</a></i>, began in July 1962 and is still broadcasting today. Such programming helped to influence in the changing social structure of Ireland. Telef\xc3\xads \xc3\x89ireann began to explore children\'s television at this point producing the groundbreaking show <a href="/wiki/Wanderly_Wagon" title="Wanderly Wagon">Wanderly Wagon</a> which inspired a generation with characters like Judge and Mr Crow.\n</p>\n<dl><dt>1970s</dt>\n<dd></dd></dl>\n<p>In 1978, the Government of Ireland approved the launch of a second public service channel to be operated by RT\xc3\x89. <a href="/wiki/RT%C3%89_Two" class="mw-redirect" title="RT\xc3\x89 Two">RT\xc3\x892</a> (later rebranded as Network 2 in 1988 and renamed RT\xc3\x89 Two in 2004) had a public service remit providing Irish-language services, while also offering alternative services - mainly programming from the US and UK.\n</p>\n<dl><dt>1990s</dt>\n<dd></dd></dl>\n<p>During the 1990s similar to other European broadcasters RT\xc3\x89 began to expand its services to provide regional variations. RT\xc3\x89 developed its only major studio complex outside Dublin in <a href="/wiki/Cork_(city)" title="Cork (city)">Cork</a>. <a href="/w/index.php?title=RT%C3%89_Cork&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="RT\xc3\x89 Cork (page does not exist)">RT\xc3\x89 Cork</a>, opened in 1995 and became a huge success. It also became a large contributor to network output on both Radio One and RT\xc3\x89 One. Also in 1995, RT\xc3\x89 opened a regional broadcasting studio in Limerick for broadcasts in the Limerick area. In 1996, an Irish-language television service was launched <a href="/wiki/TG4" title="TG4">TG4</a> (previously Teilif\xc3\xads na Gaeilge) was launched from <a href="/wiki/Galway" title="Galway">Galway</a>. While RT\xc3\x89 provided Irish-language services such as news bulletins (<i>Nuacht</i>) and the long-running documentary series <i>L\xc3\xa9argas</i>.\n</p>\n<dl><dt>2000s</dt>\n<dd></dd></dl>\n<p>RT\xc3\x89 Television began to expand is output through the development of digital television. RT\xc3\x89 Television services became widely available in <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland" title="Northern Ireland">Northern Ireland</a> via terrestrial overspill or on <a href="/wiki/Cable_TV" class="mw-redirect" title="Cable TV">cable</a> (coverage and inclusion on cable systems varies). Since 23 April 2002, (18 April 2005 in Northern Ireland) the channels have also been available via satellite on SKY; however, some sports programmes are blocked to Northern Ireland viewers due to rights issues which conflict with the UK.\n</p><p>In January 2007, RT\xc3\x89 announced plans to launch a channel, with the working title of <a href="/wiki/RT%C3%89_International" class="mw-redirect" title="RT\xc3\x89 International">RT\xc3\x89 International</a>, which would offer programmes from RT\xc3\x89 One and Two as well as TG4.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> however as of 2017 this service has still to materialise.\n</p>\n<dl><dt>2010s</dt>\n<dd></dd></dl>\n<p>On 26 May 2011, RT\xc3\x89 television launched the public service Mux for digital terrestrial television known as <a href="/wiki/Saorview" title="Saorview">Saorview</a> and <a href="/wiki/Saorsat" title="Saorsat">Saorsat</a>. RT\xc3\x89 also launched <a href="/wiki/RT%C3%89_Two" class="mw-redirect" title="RT\xc3\x89 Two">RT\xc3\x89 Two</a> HD, <a href="/wiki/RT%C3%89jr" title="RT\xc3\x89jr">RT\xc3\x89jr</a>, <a href="/wiki/RT%C3%89_One" title="RT\xc3\x89 One">RT\xc3\x89 One</a>+1 and <a href="/wiki/RT%C3%89_News_Now" class="mw-redirect" title="RT\xc3\x89 News Now">RT\xc3\x89 News Now</a> on Saorview on the same day.\n<br />\nFor the 50th anniversary of the start of RT\xc3\x89 television <a href="/wiki/John_Bowman_(broadcaster)" title="John Bowman (broadcaster)">John Bowman</a> produced a history of RT\xc3\x89 Television titled: <i>Window and Mirror. RT\xc3\x89 Television: 1961\xe2\x80\x932011</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> which was launched by <a href="/wiki/Taoiseach" title="Taoiseach">Taoiseach</a> <a href="/wiki/Enda_Kenny" title="Enda Kenny">Enda Kenny</a> at the National Museum in Dublin on 23 November 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>\n<br />\nAt 10:00&#160;am on 24 October 2012 all analogue television transmissions ended in Ireland,<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> and RT\xc3\x89\'s television channels are now only available digitally on <a href="/wiki/Saorview" title="Saorview">Saorview</a>, satellite, and cable. Also on 24 October 2012, for the first time RT\xc3\x89 1 and RT\xc3\x89 2 were broadcast from transmitters within Northern Ireland on the UK <a href="/wiki/Freeview_(UK)" title="Freeview (UK)">Freeview</a> system.\n</p><p>In December 2014, RT\xc3\x89 made <a href="/wiki/Television_advertising" class="mw-redirect" title="Television advertising">television advertising</a> history by airing the first-ever native HD advert in the UK and Ireland. The commercial was part of the <a href="/wiki/3_Mobile" class="mw-redirect" title="3 Mobile">3 Mobile</a> Christmas campaign. It was created by Dublin <a href="/wiki/Creative_agency" class="mw-redirect" title="Creative agency">creative agency</a> Boys &amp; Girls and was delivered by global delivery specialists IMD.<sup id="cite_ref-RT\xc3\x89_Score_a_First_in_HD_Ad_Delivery_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RT\xc3\x89_Score_a_First_in_HD_Ad_Delivery-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="News">News</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Raidi%C3%B3_Teilif%C3%ADs_%C3%89ireann&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: News">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/RT%C3%89_News_and_Current_Affairs" title="RT\xc3\x89 News and Current Affairs">RT\xc3\x89 News and Current Affairs</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:RT%C3%89_Outside_Broadcast_Unit_December_2009_2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/RT%C3%89_Outside_Broadcast_Unit_December_2009_2.jpg/220px-RT%C3%89_Outside_Broadcast_Unit_December_2009_2.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/RT%C3%89_Outside_Broadcast_Unit_December_2009_2.jpg/330px-RT%C3%89_Outside_Broadcast_Unit_December_2009_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/RT%C3%89_Outside_Broadcast_Unit_December_2009_2.jpg/440px-RT%C3%89_Outside_Broadcast_Unit_December_2009_2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5616" data-file-height="3744" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:RT%C3%89_Outside_Broadcast_Unit_December_2009_2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An RT\xc3\x89 satellite van</div></div></div>\n<p><i>RT\xc3\x89 News and Current Affairs</i>, or <i>Nuacht agus C\xc3\xbarsa\xc3\xad Reatha RT\xc3\x89</i> in Irish, is a major division of Raidi\xc3\xb3 Teilif\xc3\xads \xc3\x89ireann responsible for news programming on television, radio and online within Ireland. It is, by far, the largest and most popular news source in Ireland&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 with 77% of the Irish public regarding it as their main source of both Irish and international news.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2009)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup><sup id="cite_ref-RT\xc3\x89_News_and_Current_Affairs_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RT\xc3\x89_News_and_Current_Affairs-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> It broadcasts in both the Irish and English languages, as well as <a href="/wiki/Irish_Sign_Language" title="Irish Sign Language">Irish Sign Language</a>.\n</p><p>RT\xc3\x89 News and Current Affairs provides a range of national and international news and current affairs programming in Ireland. The organisation is also a source of commentary on current affairs. RT\xc3\x89 News is based at the RT\xc3\x89 Television Complex at Montrose in <a href="/wiki/Donnybrook,_Dublin" title="Donnybrook, Dublin">Donnybrook, Dublin</a>, Ireland. However, the station also operates regional bureaux across Ireland and the world.\n</p><p>RT\xc3\x89 News faces competition from within Ireland and abroad. Within Ireland, competition is provided by <a href="/wiki/TV3_News" class="mw-redirect" title="TV3 News">3News</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nuacht_TG4" title="Nuacht TG4">Nuacht TG4</a> in the television sector and <a href="/wiki/Communicorp" title="Communicorp">Communicorp</a> in the radio sector. <a href="/wiki/BBC_Newsline" title="BBC Newsline">BBC Newsline</a> and <a href="/wiki/UTV_Live" title="UTV Live">UTV Live</a> provide alternative news services from Northern Ireland, whilst global news channels are widely available, such as <a href="/wiki/Euronews" title="Euronews">Euronews</a>, <a href="/wiki/CNN_International" title="CNN International">CNN International</a>, <a href="/wiki/CNBC" title="CNBC">CNBC</a>, <a href="/wiki/France_24" title="France 24">France 24</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bloomberg_L.P." title="Bloomberg L.P.">Bloomberg</a>, <a href="/wiki/BBC_World_News" title="BBC World News">BBC World News</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sky_News" title="Sky News">Sky News</a> among many others.\n</p><p>RT\xc3\x89 News and Current Affairs produces over 1,000 hours of television programming and 2,000 hours of radio programming a year.<sup id="cite_ref-Hayes,_Maurice_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hayes,_Maurice-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the 1970s, Sinn F\xc3\xa9in the Workers Party, (the political wing of the Official IRA), were said to have progressively infiltrated RT\xc3\x89\'s Current Affairs Department, through the Ned Stapleton Cumman, which was organised by <a href="/wiki/Eoghan_Harris" title="Eoghan Harris">Eoghan Harris</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Hayes,_Maurice_52-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hayes,_Maurice-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>RT\xc3\x89\'s gaffe in January 2009 over the need for IMF intervention in the Republic was picked up by news wires. Bloomberg noted how German stocks fell sharply, while Reuters reported that the euro dipped by a cent against the dollar before it stabilised following a strong denial.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>RT\xc3\x89\'s producers and researchers were accused by journalist <a href="/wiki/Kevin_Myers" title="Kevin Myers">Kevin Myers</a> of imposing a liberal agenda, firstly on one another, and later on the airwaves, but without consciously intending to do so.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> RT\xc3\x89 News has also been described by him as behaving like a press officer for public sector unions.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">Sport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Raidi%C3%B3_Teilif%C3%ADs_%C3%89ireann&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Sport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/RT%C3%89_Sport" title="RT\xc3\x89 Sport">RT\xc3\x89 Sport</a></div>\n<p>RT\xc3\x89 is a major broadcaster of sports programming in Ireland. <a href="/wiki/Gaelic_football" title="Gaelic football">Gaelic football</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hurling" title="Hurling">hurling</a>, football and rugby are all broadcast live on radio and television and increasingly online. The broadcaster also transmits live golf, boxing, athletics, horse-racing and show-jumping and other minority sports, usually when there is a significant Irish participant(s), or the event is in Ireland. The broadcaster has secured many events, <a href="/wiki/Free-to-air" title="Free-to-air">free-to-air</a> which might otherwise become pay-per-view.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Weather">Weather</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Raidi%C3%B3_Teilif%C3%ADs_%C3%89ireann&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Weather">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Weather forecasts are provided at the end of most news on radio and television. <a href="/wiki/Met_%C3%89ireann" title="Met \xc3\x89ireann">Met \xc3\x89ireann</a> have been providing the forecasts since 1948 to Radio \xc3\x89ireann and from 1962 on television broadcasts.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Internet">Internet</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Raidi%C3%B3_Teilif%C3%ADs_%C3%89ireann&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Internet">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/RT%C3%89.ie" title="RT\xc3\x89.ie">RT\xc3\x89.ie</a></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/URL" title="URL">URL</a> \'RTE.ie\' is the brand name and home of RT\xc3\x89\'s online activities. The site began publishing on 26 May 1996. It operates on an entirely commercial basis, receiving none of the licence fee which funds much of RT\xc3\x89\'s activity.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> The site is funded by advertising and section sponsorship. As of 2007<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Raidi%C3%B3_Teilif%C3%ADs_%C3%89ireann&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, it is among the top 5,000 most visited websites globally, by <a href="/wiki/Alexa_Internet" title="Alexa Internet">Alexa</a> rankings<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> and among the top 20 sites in Ireland,<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> with certified impressions of almost 40&#160;million per month and more than 1.5&#160;million unique users.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> The most recent revamp of the website took place on 30 January 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In recent years RT\xc3\x89 has been expanding its web broadcasting capabilities. With improved access to online material and better methods of delivery, there is now a comprehensive range of services online. RT\xc3\x89 streams all of its radio stations online, including digital, and there is a web-only TV channel, <a href="/wiki/RT%C3%89_News_Now" class="mw-redirect" title="RT\xc3\x89 News Now">RT\xc3\x89 News Now</a><sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> as well as the availability to watch live programmes, subject to copyright.\n</p>\n<h3><span id="RT.C3.89_Player"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="RT\xc3\x89_Player">RT\xc3\x89 Player</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Raidi%C3%B3_Teilif%C3%ADs_%C3%89ireann&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: RT\xc3\x89 Player">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>On Tuesday 21 April 2009, RT\xc3\x89 launched its on-demand service the <a href="/wiki/RT%C3%89_Player" title="RT\xc3\x89 Player">RT\xc3\x89 Player</a>. The service allows broadband users in the Republic of Ireland to view some of RT\xc3\x89\'s top rated homegrown (i.e. <a href="/wiki/RT%C3%89_News" class="mw-redirect" title="RT\xc3\x89 News">RT\xc3\x89 News</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Late_Late_Show_(Ireland)" class="mw-redirect" title="The Late Late Show (Ireland)">The Late Late Show</a></i>) and international (i.e. <i><a href="/wiki/Home_and_Away" title="Home and Away">Home and Away</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Grey%27s_Anatomy" title="Grey&#39;s Anatomy">Grey\'s Anatomy</a></i>) TV series for free up to 21 days after its initial broadcast. A cut-down version is available outside Ireland.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="RT.C3.89_and_Netflix"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="RT\xc3\x89_and_Netflix">RT\xc3\x89 and Netflix</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Raidi%C3%B3_Teilif%C3%ADs_%C3%89ireann&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: RT\xc3\x89 and Netflix">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>On Thursday, 13 September 2012: RT\xc3\x89 Digital confirmed<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> that it has signed a deal with <a href="/wiki/Netflix" title="Netflix">Netflix</a> to host its programming. Episodes of RT\xc3\x89 television dramas and comedies, including <i><a href="/wiki/The_Clinic_(TV_series)" title="The Clinic (TV series)">The Clinic</a></i>, <i>Trivia</i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Killinaskully" title="Killinaskully">Killinaskully</a></i>, and <i>Mattie</i>, will be added to Netflix and available outside Ireland under a new deal between the broadcaster and the online subscription service.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_activities">Other activities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Raidi%C3%B3_Teilif%C3%ADs_%C3%89ireann&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Other activities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Digital">Digital</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Raidi%C3%B3_Teilif%C3%ADs_%C3%89ireann&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Digital">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/RT%C3%89.ie" title="RT\xc3\x89.ie">RT\xc3\x89.ie</a> and <a href="/wiki/RT%C3%89_Aertel" title="RT\xc3\x89 Aertel">RT\xc3\x89 Aertel</a></div>\n<p><i>RT\xc3\x89 Digital</i> division replaced the RT\xc3\x89 Publishing division in 2012 and operates six media services \n</p>\n<ul><li><i>RTE.ie</i> \xe2\x80\x93 providing online news, sport, and entertainment services</li>\n<li><i>RT\xc3\x89 Player/RT\xc3\x89 Radio Player</i> \xe2\x80\x93 on demand and live streams of all of RT\xc3\x89\'s national radio and TV networks</li>\n<li><i>RT\xc3\x89 Aertel</i> \xe2\x80\x93 teletext service which has news, sport, and programme support information</li>\n<li><i>RT\xc3\x89 News Now App</i> \xe2\x80\x93 live/catch-up news service, online and on mobile</li>\n<li><i>RT\xc3\x89 Archives</i> \xe2\x80\x93 central repository for all RT\xc3\x89 broadcast (Television and Radio) and stills material collected and preserved by RT\xc3\x89</li></ul>\n<p>Areas of responsibility\n</p>\n<ul><li>Sale of music copyright</li>\n<li>Maintenance of Television channel archives and news library</li>\n<li>Sale of library and archive material</li>\n<li>Maintenance of Radio channel archive and library</li>\n<li>Provision of RT\xc3\x89 Aertel teletext services</li>\n<li>Provision of a range of free to public, public service web-based Online services</li>\n<li>Operation of the RT\xc3\x89 Player to domestic and international audiences</li>\n<li>Sale of online banner advertising and sponsorship</li>\n<li>Sale of teletext advertising and sponsorship</li>\n<li>Commercial Telecoms revenue</li>\n<li>Incubation and development of new media technologies</li>\n<li>Administration of RT\xc3\x89 Digital IBD</li>\n<li>Provision of additional opportunities to access RT\xc3\x89\'s public service news content via RT\xc3\x89 News Now Online</li></ul>\n<h3><span id="Orchestras_Quartet_.26_Choirs"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Orchestras_Quartet_&amp;_Choirs">Orchestras Quartet &amp; Choirs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Raidi%C3%B3_Teilif%C3%ADs_%C3%89ireann&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Orchestras Quartet &amp; Choirs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/RT%C3%89_Performing_Groups" title="RT\xc3\x89 Performing Groups">RT\xc3\x89 Performing Groups</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:RT%C3%89_National_Symphony_Orchestra_Image.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/RT%C3%89_National_Symphony_Orchestra_Image.png/220px-RT%C3%89_National_Symphony_Orchestra_Image.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="181" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/RT%C3%89_National_Symphony_Orchestra_Image.png/330px-RT%C3%89_National_Symphony_Orchestra_Image.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/RT%C3%89_National_Symphony_Orchestra_Image.png/440px-RT%C3%89_National_Symphony_Orchestra_Image.png 2x" data-file-width="501" data-file-height="412" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:RT%C3%89_National_Symphony_Orchestra_Image.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The RT\xc3\x89 National Symphony Orchestra</div></div></div>\n<p><i>RT\xc3\x89 Orchestras Quartet &amp; Choirs</i> supports two full-time orchestras\xe2\x80\x94the RT\xc3\x89 Concert Orchestra and RT\xc3\x89 National Symphony Orchestra\xe2\x80\x94as well as the RT\xc3\x89 Vanbrugh Quartet, RT\xc3\x89 Philharmonic Choir, and RT\xc3\x89 C\xc3\xb3r na n\xc3\x93g. These groups perform regularly in the <a href="/wiki/National_Concert_Hall" title="National Concert Hall">National Concert Hall</a> and <a href="/wiki/The_Helix_(Dublin)" class="mw-redirect" title="The Helix (Dublin)">The Helix</a> in Dublin. The five groups present over 250 events annually, including live performances and work in education. The RT\xc3\x89 NSO and the RT\xc3\x89 CO employ a total of 134 professional musicians. The RT\xc3\x89 Philharmonic Choir and the children\'s choir RT\xc3\x89 C\xc3\xb3r na n\xc3\x93g are for singers at an amateur level. Currently, approximately 200 adults and children are involved in the choirs.\n</p>\n<ul><li>Performing Groups\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/RT%C3%89_National_Symphony_Orchestra" title="RT\xc3\x89 National Symphony Orchestra">RT\xc3\x89 National Symphony Orchestra</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/RT%C3%89_Concert_Orchestra" title="RT\xc3\x89 Concert Orchestra">RT\xc3\x89 Concert Orchestra</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/RT%C3%89_Philharmonic_Choir" title="RT\xc3\x89 Philharmonic Choir">RT\xc3\x89 Philharmonic Choir</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/RT%C3%89_C%C3%B3r_na_n%C3%93g" title="RT\xc3\x89 C\xc3\xb3r na n\xc3\x93g">RT\xc3\x89 C\xc3\xb3r na n\xc3\x93g</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/RT%C3%89_Vanbrugh_Quartet" title="RT\xc3\x89 Vanbrugh Quartet">RT\xc3\x89 Vanbrugh Quartet</a></li></ul></li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Infrastructure">Infrastructure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Raidi%C3%B3_Teilif%C3%ADs_%C3%89ireann&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Infrastructure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p><i><a href="/wiki/2RN_(RT%C3%89_Networks)" title="2RN (RT\xc3\x89 Networks)">RT\xc3\x89 Networks</a></i> (branded as 2RN) is operated through a wholly owned subsidiary company, <a href="/wiki/2RN_(RT%C3%89_Networks)" title="2RN (RT\xc3\x89 Networks)">RT\xc3\x89 Network Transmission Limited</a>, and provides transmission services for all of RT\xc3\x89\'s own channels and also for competing stations such as <a href="/wiki/TV3_(Ireland)" class="mw-redirect" title="TV3 (Ireland)">TV3 Ireland</a>, <a href="/wiki/TG4" title="TG4">TG4</a> and <a href="/wiki/Today_FM" title="Today FM">Today FM</a>.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Saorview">Saorview</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Raidi%C3%B3_Teilif%C3%ADs_%C3%89ireann&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Saorview">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Saorview" title="Saorview">Saorview</a></div>\n<p><i>Saorview</i>, founded by <a href="/wiki/2RN_(RT%C3%89_Networks)" title="2RN (RT\xc3\x89 Networks)">2RN</a>, is the name for the Irish FTA DTT.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> The service was launched as a trial service on 31 October 2010 to 90% of the population and it was officially launched on 26 May 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> Set-top boxes for the service are available<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> By legislation it must be available nationwide by December 2011. The service is free although a MPEG-4 DVB-T box and a UHF aerial will be needed although some newer TV sets have MPEG-4 DVB-T decoders built into the TV set which do not need a separate box. 2RN can provide for commercial DTT capacity on its network for any <a href="/wiki/Television_in_Ireland#Historical_testing" class="mw-redirect" title="Television in Ireland">pay TV service</a> that can agree terms with it and the BAI. However that is likely until 2013 according to the BAI following on from a de-briefing exercise the BAI held with the three consortia involved in the 2008 failed license process. The BAI said "the Authority now considers that it will not be feasible to introduce commercial DTT as originally intended until after Analogue Switch Off (ASO) at the earliest. The position will be reviewed towards the end of 2011 and the Authority may seek expressions of interest in the provision of commercial DTT at that point. A competition could potentially be held during 2012 with a view to commercial DTT being operational in 2013." It continued "it is the considered view of the Authority that as part of the preparation for the successful launch of commercial DTT in the future, legislative change will be necessary to enable the Authority to have formal relationships with the applicants, as obtains at present, and with RT\xc3\x89NL."<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup><br />\nAnalogue television transmission was ended on 24 October 2012 and Saorview became the primary source of Irish terrestrial television.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Saorsat">Saorsat</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Raidi%C3%B3_Teilif%C3%ADs_%C3%89ireann&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Saorsat">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p><i>Saorsat</i><sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> is the proposed name for the <a href="/wiki/Free-to-air" title="Free-to-air">free-to-air</a> <a href="/w/index.php?title=Digital_satellite_television&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Digital satellite television (page does not exist)">digital satellite television</a> service in Ireland is expected that RT\xc3\x89 will use a new satellite service to broadcast to homes in more remote areas of Ireland with the possibility of broadband provision by June 2011. On 14 July 2010 RT\xc3\x89 NL outlined detailed plans for the <a href="/wiki/Digital_terrestrial_television" title="Digital terrestrial television">digital terrestrial television</a> (DTT) infrastructure project and digital satellite television (DST) using Ka narrowband, which will see the shut-down of the existing analogue system and launch of a domestic-only satellite service for the first time since establishment of RT\xc3\x89 covering the area not possible due to terrain issues by DTT.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Library">Library</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Raidi%C3%B3_Teilif%C3%ADs_%C3%89ireann&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Library">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/RT%C3%89_Libraries_and_Archives" title="RT\xc3\x89 Libraries and Archives">RT\xc3\x89 Libraries and Archives</a></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Logo">Logo</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Raidi%C3%B3_Teilif%C3%ADs_%C3%89ireann&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Logo">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In 1995, the logo dropped the Brigid\'s cross, and for the first time placed an accent (<i lang="ga" title="Irish-language text"><a href="/wiki/S%C3%ADneadh_fada" class="mw-redirect" title="S\xc3\xadneadh fada">fada</a></i>) on the letter E. RT\xc3\x89 also formal branded Network Two on screen as part of RT\xc3\x89 until 1997, when the channel was once more re-branded on screen as N2. The three letters are a modern take on <a href="/wiki/Celtic_script" class="mw-redirect" title="Celtic script">Celtic scripting</a>. The Brigid\'s cross was seen on many RT\xc3\x89 One television idents until 2003 and remains on the <a href="/wiki/Headed_paper" class="mw-redirect" title="Headed paper">headed paper</a> of RT\xc3\x89, while a variation of the 1966 cross is used by RT\xc3\x89\'s Graphic Design Department.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> Since 2004 all RT\xc3\x89 service use the 1996 logo as part of their Identity.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2015, RT\xc3\x89 re-branded its network following a tending process introduced in February 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> In 2015 RT\xc3\x89 Archives launched a new logo which incorporated the 1969 branding for the word "Archive".\n</p>\n<h2><span id="Controversies_involving_RT.C3.89"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Controversies_involving_RT\xc3\x89">Controversies involving RT\xc3\x89</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Raidi%C3%B3_Teilif%C3%ADs_%C3%89ireann&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Controversies involving RT\xc3\x89">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Competition_cases">Competition cases</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Raidi%C3%B3_Teilif%C3%ADs_%C3%89ireann&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Competition cases">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In 2006, RT\xc3\x89 was involved in a <a href="/wiki/High_Court_of_Ireland" class="mw-redirect" title="High Court of Ireland">High Court</a> case relating to <a href="/wiki/Referential_bid" title="Referential bid">referential bidding</a> in relation to sponsoring weather forecasts: <i>Smart Telecom PLC trading as </i>Smart Telecom<i> v Raidi\xc3\xb3 Teilif\xc3\xads \xc3\x89ireann and by order Glanbia PLC</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In October 2011, RT\xc3\x89 was forced to stop a "share deal" scheme it had offered advertisers when TV3 complained to the <a href="/wiki/Competition_Authority_(Ireland)" title="Competition Authority (Ireland)">Competition Authority</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Death_of_Gerry_Ryan">Death of Gerry Ryan</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Raidi%C3%B3_Teilif%C3%ADs_%C3%89ireann&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Death of Gerry Ryan">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Death_of_Gerry_Ryan" title="Death of Gerry Ryan">death of Gerry Ryan</a> led to controversy for RT\xc3\x89 when it emerged that traces of cocaine were the "likely trigger" of the star\'s sudden death on 30 April 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Minister_for_Children,_Equality,_Disability,_Integration_and_Youth" title="Minister for Children, Equality, Disability, Integration and Youth">Drugs Minister</a> <a href="/wiki/Pat_Carey" title="Pat Carey">Pat Carey</a> said he was "a bit taken aback, first of all, by the whole attitude of RT\xc3\x89 over the last while" concerning the circumstances of Ryan\'s death. Comparing Ryan\'s cocaine use to the 2007 death of model <a href="/wiki/Katy_French" title="Katy French">Katy French</a>, Carey said that the media were "very judgmental" when French died but had now "come home to roost in their own case".<sup id="cite_ref-Minister_\xe2\x80\x98taken_aback\xe2\x80\x99_at_RT\xc3\x89\xe2\x80\x99s_silence_over_Ryan_death_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Minister_\xe2\x80\x98taken_aback\xe2\x80\x99_at_RT\xc3\x89\xe2\x80\x99s_silence_over_Ryan_death-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Defamation_cases">Defamation cases</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Raidi%C3%B3_Teilif%C3%ADs_%C3%89ireann&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Defamation cases">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In 2011, RT\xc3\x89 was sued for defamation after making false allegations about a priest.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> On 23 May 2011, RT\xc3\x89 had aired a <i><a href="/wiki/Prime_Time_(Irish_TV_programme)" title="Prime Time (Irish TV programme)">Prime Time Investigates</a></i> programme called <i><a href="/wiki/Mission_to_Prey" title="Mission to Prey">Mission to Prey</a></i>, which falsely claimed that the priest had raped a woman and fathered her child while working as a <a href="/wiki/Missionary" title="Missionary">missionary</a> in <a href="/wiki/Kenya" title="Kenya">Kenya</a>. In October 2011, RT\xc3\x89 issued a public apology, stating that the allegations were baseless and should never have been broadcast.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> The priest said he had been "living a nightmare" after the broadcaster made the allegations.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> The issue was serious enough to be discussed in both houses of the <a href="/wiki/Oireachtas" title="Oireachtas">Oireachtas</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> In November 2011, the priest concerned reached an out-of-court settlement with RT\xc3\x89, in which RT\xc3\x89 agreed that it had seriously <a href="/wiki/Libel" class="mw-redirect" title="Libel">libelled</a> him, and paid the priest a significant amount of money in damages. As a consequence, managing director of news Ed Mulhall retired, current affairs editor Ken O\'Shea was moved to another department, and reporter <a href="/wiki/Aoife_Kavanagh" title="Aoife Kavanagh">Aoife Kavanagh</a> resigned. The affair was described as "one of the gravest editorial mistakes ever made" in RT\xc3\x89\'s history.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Moral_controversies">Moral controversies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Raidi%C3%B3_Teilif%C3%ADs_%C3%89ireann&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Moral controversies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p><i><a href="/wiki/The_Late_Late_Show_(Ireland)" class="mw-redirect" title="The Late Late Show (Ireland)">The Late Late Show</a></i> has been involved in a number of controversies since first being broadcast on TV in July 1962, particularly during <a href="/wiki/Gay_Byrne" title="Gay Byrne">Gay Byrne</a>\'s tenure, with the "Bishop and the Nightie Affair" in 1966 and a 1985 interview with a pair of lesbian former nuns which led to protesters picketing the studio with hymns and rosary beads after a <a href="/wiki/High_Court_(Ireland)" title="High Court (Ireland)">High Court</a> case during which there were calls for the chat show to be outlawed over fears it would "greatly undermine Christian moral values" and "the respect of the general public for nuns".<sup id="cite_ref-sex_factor_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sex_factor-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> Notorious incidents during <a href="/wiki/Pat_Kenny" title="Pat Kenny">Pat Kenny</a>\'s tenure included a satanic dance troupe performance and the tearing up of two tickets for <i><a href="/wiki/The_Late_Late_Toy_Show" title="The Late Late Toy Show">The Late Late Toy Show</a></i> live on air.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The first sex scandal on Irish TV surrounded a sketch-drawing advert for <a href="/wiki/Bri-Nylon" class="mw-redirect" title="Bri-Nylon">Bri-Nylon</a> underwear, involving a "lewd and lascivious" cartoon of <a href="/wiki/Mark_Antony" title="Mark Antony">Antony</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cleopatra" title="Cleopatra">Cleopatra</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-sex_factor_92-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sex_factor-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Wesley Burroughs received a dressing down from RT\xc3\x89 authorities after it became apparent actress Biddy White Lennon, who portrayed the character Maggie Riordan, was becoming increasingly more pregnant looking every week on <i><a href="/wiki/The_Riordans" title="The Riordans">The Riordans</a></i>, an RT\xc3\x89 soap opera he wrote for. Maggie Riordan was an unmarried woman. Burroughs was forced to consult medical texts to provide Maggie with an alternative illness.<sup id="cite_ref-sex_factor_92-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sex_factor-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The TV drama series <i><a href="/wiki/The_Spike_(TV_series)" title="The Spike (TV series)">The Spike</a></i>, broadcast on RT\xc3\x89 in 1978, was involved in a sex scandal.<sup id="cite_ref-sex_factor_92-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sex_factor-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1986, <a href="/wiki/Mandy_Smith" title="Mandy Smith">Mandy Smith</a> was to be interviewed on TV\'s <i>Saturday Live</i> until RT\xc3\x89 decided she should be downgraded to being a mere member of the audience. She was axed entirely when her manager disagreed, with RT\xc3\x89 saying she was "not important enough" and that she might "give a bad example to young teenage girls". The story appeared in the international media.<sup id="cite_ref-sex_factor_92-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sex_factor-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Political_controversies">Political controversies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Raidi%C3%B3_Teilif%C3%ADs_%C3%89ireann&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Political controversies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In 2009, RT\xc3\x89 apologised to the then <a href="/wiki/Taoiseach" title="Taoiseach">Taoiseach</a> <a href="/wiki/Brian_Cowen" title="Brian Cowen">Brian Cowen</a> for its role in the <a href="/wiki/Brian_Cowen_nude_portraits_controversy" title="Brian Cowen nude portraits controversy">Brian Cowen nude portraits controversy</a>. Future Taoiseach <a href="/wiki/Enda_Kenny" title="Enda Kenny">Enda Kenny</a><sup id="cite_ref-Ceann_Comhairle_exasperated_as_Kenny_fails_to_see_the_bigger_picture_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ceann_Comhairle_exasperated_as_Kenny_fails_to_see_the_bigger_picture-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Charles_Flanagan" title="Charles Flanagan">Charles Flanagan</a> called RT\xc3\x89\'s backtracking a restriction on <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_speech" title="Freedom of speech">freedom of expression</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Teacher_questioned_over_Cowen_paintings_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Teacher_questioned_over_Cowen_paintings-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Opposition_slams_Govt_over_portrait_pressure_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Opposition_slams_Govt_over_portrait_pressure-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Liz_McManus" title="Liz McManus">Liz McManus</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Labour_Party_(Ireland)" title="Labour Party (Ireland)">Labour Party</a> criticised RT\xc3\x89 for "bow[ing] to political pressure".<sup id="cite_ref-Opposition_slams_Govt_over_portrait_pressure_96-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Opposition_slams_Govt_over_portrait_pressure-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In September 2010, RT\xc3\x89 broadcast a controversial nine-minute radio interview with Taoiseach <a href="/wiki/Brian_Cowen" title="Brian Cowen">Brian Cowen</a> from a <a href="/wiki/Fianna_F%C3%A1il" title="Fianna F\xc3\xa1il">Fianna F\xc3\xa1il</a> think-in in <a href="/wiki/Galway" title="Galway">Galway</a>. The interview led to increased pressure for Cowen to resign in the days that followed after it was thought he had been drunk on the radio.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 24 October 2011, three days before the <a href="/wiki/2011_Irish_presidential_election" title="2011 Irish presidential election">2011 Irish presidential election</a>, RT\xc3\x89 hosted the final presidential debate on <a href="/wiki/Pat_Kenny" title="Pat Kenny">Pat Kenny</a>\'s <i><a href="/wiki/The_Frontline_(Irish_TV_programme)" title="The Frontline (Irish TV programme)">The Frontline</a></i>, in which it controversially broadcast an unverified <a href="/wiki/Twitter" title="Twitter">tweet</a> mid-debate which was widely seen as damaging to the frontrunner candidate <a href="/wiki/Se%C3%A1n_Gallagher" title="Se\xc3\xa1n Gallagher">Se\xc3\xa1n Gallagher</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-patl_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-patl-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> Gallagher had been the frontrunner in an opinion poll at this point.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> On election day, Gallagher received 28.5% of first preference votes in the election, leaving him in second place behind <a href="/wiki/Michael_D._Higgins" title="Michael D. Higgins">Michael D. Higgins</a>. <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a></i>, chronicling the reasons for Gallagher\'s fall in support, reported that a final RT\xc3\x89 poll showed that 28% of Irish voters had changed their mind in the last week of the campaign, with 58% of those switching from Gallagher.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> On 7 March 2012, the Irish <a href="/wiki/Broadcasting_Authority_of_Ireland" title="Broadcasting Authority of Ireland">Broadcasting Authority of Ireland</a> upheld Gallagher\'s complaint about unfair treatment regarding how RT\xc3\x89 handled the unverified tweet on the final Pat Kenny debate.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup>  On 19 December 2017, it was reported that RT\xc3\x89 had agreed to pay Gallagher a sum of \xe2\x82\xac130,000 as part of a confidential legal settlement arising from the debate.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Raidi%C3%B3_Teilif%C3%ADs_%C3%89ireann&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/List_of_programmes_broadcast_by_RT%C3%89" class="mw-redirect" title="List of programmes broadcast by RT\xc3\x89">List of programmes broadcast by RT\xc3\x89</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Television_in_Ireland" class="mw-redirect" title="Television in Ireland">Television in Ireland</a></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Further_reading">Further reading</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Raidi%C3%B3_Teilif%C3%ADs_%C3%89ireann&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Further reading">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<ul><li>Jack Dowling, <a href="/wiki/Lelia_Doolan" title="Lelia Doolan">Lelia Doolan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bob_Quinn_(Irish_filmmaker)" class="mw-redirect" title="Bob Quinn (Irish filmmaker)">Bob Quinn</a>, <i>Sit Down and be Counted: the cultural evolution of a television station</i>, Wellington Publishers Ltd., Dublin, 1969.</li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a
